Introductory Remarks
The manuscript of the Tibetan Kanjur written some time between A.D. 1696 and
1706 in the West Tibetan monastery of Phug brag is one of the most valuable
treasures' housed in the Library of Tibetan Works & Archives (LTWA), Dha-
ramsala. In 1987 the Tibetan authorities entered on a joint venture with the
Institute for Advanced Studies of World Religions (IASWR), New York. The
aim was to prepare a microform edition of the Phug brag Kanjur and to make
it accessible to scholars world-wide. Jampa Samten, then Chief Librarian of the
Manuscript Section in the LTWA, assisted by Lobsang Shastri, was responsible
for the microfilming in Dharamsala.
At about the same time JAMPA SAMTEN started compiling a descriptive
catalogue of the Kanjur manuscript from Phug brag. In 1990 the first copies of
the microfiche edition were issued by the IASWR, New York. The catalogue
prepared by JAMPA SAMTEN was published under the title Phug brag bka' 'gyur
bris ma'i dkar chag/A Catalogue of the Phug-brag Manuscript Kanjur by the
LTWA in Dharamsala in 1992. The present "Location List" is meant to serve
practical purposes only, directing the reader to the various texts in the
microform edition of the Phug brag Kanjur; for JAMPA SAMTEN's catalogue re-
fers to the manuscript only and does not give the exact location of the individual
texts in the microform edition, which in turn does not include the folio numbers
found in the headlines of the microfiche cards.
In general, JAMPA SAMTEN describes the Kanjur manuscript prepared in the
Phug brag Monastery in accordance with the accompanying Tibetan catalogue
Three studies have been undertaken so far showing the value of this source, viz. HAHN,
HARRISON, and SCHOENING,
? A first announcement of this microform edition appeared in the Publications Catalog issued
by the IASWR in September 1986.



Introductory Remarks
(dkar chag) entitled Bka' 'gyur rin po che' dkar char gsal ba' me lon. The
microfiche edition conforms to this pattern as regards both the arrangement of
the sections and the order of the volumes within the sections. But in several
instances the manuscript and the Dkar chag do not agree with each other. A case
in point is the Tibetan Saddharmasmrtyupasthänasūtra, which the Dkar chag lists
as comprising volumes ya (24), ra (25), la (26), and śa (27) of the Mdo section.
In the manuscript the four volumes are marked by the marginal letters ya (24),
ra (25), ra (25), and śa (27), i.e. the last portion of the text in question is
separated from the main body by a full intermediate volume, viz. volume la
(26).
In cataloguing the Kanjur manuscript JAMPA SAMTEN provides the indi-
vidual texts with running numbers. Among these the number 11 occurs three
times, as three versions of the Tibetan Astasahasrika Prajñāpāramita have been
incorporated. Both the Sanskrit Prajñāpāramitahrdayasūtra and its ensuing Tibe-
tan version are assigned the number 13. In the case of the above-mentioned
Tibetan Saddharmasmrtyupasthānasūtra (in volumes 77 to 79, and 81) and of the
Tibetan Karmasaraka (in volumes 83 and 97) JAMPA SAMTEN attributes a
second number to the continuations, thus the former consists of nos. 230 and
254, the latter of nos. 269 and 402. The version of the Lokaprajñapti at the end
of volume 78 (i.e. mdo sde, ra) is listed neither in the Dkar chag nor in the
descriptive catalogue; it was found by checking the microfiche cards and is
numbered in the "Location List" as no. 230a. So there are actually two versions
of the Tibetan Lokaprajñapti in the Phug brag Kanjur, the other one being
registered under no. 403.

Each volume is represented in the microform edition by a group of microfiche
cards, the number of which ranges between 8 (in the Dkar chag volume) and 84
(in volume 54, e.g.). The microfiche cards show, above the reproduced text, an
area filled with Roman script and forming a headline. In this area the title of the
whole collection, i.e.
"Phu-brag Bka'-'gyur"
is given at the left-hand top.
Under the title are written the Tibetan name of the section and the identi-
fication letter of the volume concerned, the current number being added, e.g.,
"Mdo-sde Ke Vol. 87".
The line
"The Institute for Advanced Studies of World Religions"
separates the Roman-script area from the reproduced Tibetan text.
The right upper corner of each microfiche card contains the code
indicating the exact location of that card within the full set. This code is com-
posed of three parts. At its beginning we find "LMpj 016"; this is a specific key
used by the IASWR for classifying the material collected. In this system "L"
stands for "literature", "M" for "monographic", "p" for "printed material" and ")"
for "microjackets", while "016" refers to the set of microfiches. In the fol-
lowiog "Location List" the key "LMpj 016" is represented by "#".
The second part of the composite code, separated from the first by a
comma, consists of numerals ranging between 800 and 919. They refer to the re-
Two volumes bear the marginal letter ra, the volume ko is missing.
Not catalogued by SAMTEN.
10 This is one of the several spellings of the name of the monastery, the other ones being
Spud tra, Phu dra, Spu grags, Spu brag; for etymological reasons JAMPA SAMTEN prefers the form
Phug brag, accepted here as well, cf. SAMIEN, p. ii.
"I am indebted to Mrs. Margaret Chen, LASWR, for this information.
12 The microfiche edition of the Cone Tanjur, e.g., is counted "020", that of the Sung Chi-sha
Tsang "023", that of the Derge Kanjur "012".

Introductory Remarks
spective volume. If we subtract 799, we obtain the running number of the
volume in JAMPA SAMTEN's catalogue of the Phug brag Kanjur; 886, e.g., stands
for volume 87.
The final part of the complete code -- from volume 27 (# 826) onward it
is placed in the line above the "LMpj 016" and the volume code -- pertains to
the individual microfiche card. It indicates two things: The number before the
slash gives the position of the card within the group of microfiches forming that
particular volume; the number after the slash states the total of cards belonging
to that group.
The microfiche taken as an example has the following headline:
Phu-brag Bka'-'gyur
19/65
Mdo-sde Ke Vol. 87
LMpj 016, 886
The Institute for Advanced Studies of World Religions
In general, the individual microfiche cards contain six frames of Tibetan text
arranged in two lines of three frames each." Reading starts at the left-hand top
and passes on to the next frame to the right for continuing. This rule is not valid
for the first volume and for the first 29 cards of the second volume; there
reading begins at the right-hand side of the line and proceeds to the left. The
second line of frames is read after the first one.
Every frame shows two pages, viz. the verso of a leaf above and the recto
of the next leaf below. At the beginning and end of a volume the jackets are re-
garded as a sort of first verso and last recto respectively. According to this system
the right frame of the lower line of each card should contain the recto of a leaf
bearing the folio number six or a multiple of six, provided the volume does not
show any irregularities and no mistake has been made in filming.
As a matter of fact, the Phug brag Kanjur manuscript contains various in-
stances of irregular foliation. Several folios bear two numbers. In a few cases
more than two numbers are attributed to the same leaf. In other cases the
same folio number is applied to more than one leaf, the leaves in point being
generally differentiated by syllables like gon or 'ogle added to the number.
Moreover, in some cases the same pages were filmed twice. Therefore the posi-
tion of the folios the number of which is divisible by six can change on the
microfiches.
In the following "Location List" a capital letter is added to the number of
* Exceptions to this rule are, e.g., the microfiches # 800 1/79, # 800 2/79, and #801 28/72
showing twice two frames each. The final card of a volume contains between 1 and 6 frames.
14 Lc. up to microfiche # 801 29/72.
15 In volume 83 e.g. folio 202/232 is numbered as follows: xx gris nii (brgya grtis nas so grum
du chons, "jump from 202 to 233 [233 being the number of the ensuing leaf)".
16 Other syllables may be used as well. In the case of three folios bearing the same number,
bar may be added to the middle one.

ends. The frames of the upper line are assigned the letters A to C, those of the
lower line the letters D to F. This is illustrated by the following scheme:

The reference to an individual text within a volume consists (1) of the card
position numbers and letters for start and end, and (2) of an indication of the
total of cards within that volume added after the slash.
The headlines of chapters and paragraphs in the following "Location List" have
been taken from the section titles, from the volume letters and numbers in
JAMPA SAMTEN's catalogue, and from the headlines on the microfiche cards.
The running text numbers introduced by JAMPA SAMTEN, together with
the complete microfiche location code for starts and end of a text within
the microform edition, constitute the first line, printed in bold type, in the brief
listing of the individual texts.
The marginal letters and/or, if present, titles20 as well as the folio num-
bers for the text as culled from the microfiches are given in the second line.
The word "missing" added to a folio number has a double meaning; it may indi-
cate that the leaf in point has been skipped in foliation, or that it is actually
lacking, thus causing a gap in the text. In the case of texts continuing in the
following volume/volumes more than one location code and marginal identifi-
cation may appear, as e.g. in the 'Bum section.
In general, the titles of the texts appear in the form of the Tibetan initial
titles; if an initial title is absent, the title is supplied from the colophon or
from elsewhere, with the source indicated in parentheses. In the "Location List"
the titles are given as found in the microfiches, obvious mistakes being corrected

The brief listing of the individual text may end with a concordance line
indicating the parallel texts in four other printed or manuscript editions of the
Kanjur by means of pertinent sigla and catalogue numbers; if the same text
appears more than once in the Phug brag Kanjur, its number (printed in bold
type) precedes the sigla and numbers of the other parallels. Notes (printed in
smaller type) relate mainly to titles on title-pages, to misplaced microfiche
frames, to illegible portions of titles, to special references etc.

Introductory Remarks
For several reasons the "Location List" presented on the following pages is a
provisional one. The descriptive catalogue prepared by JAMPA SAMTEN, on
which the "Location List" relies, turned out to be not quite complete; otherwise
the basic checking of the microfiche cards would not have resulted in finding an
unrecorded text of considerable length, viz. the second copy of the Tibetan
Lokaprajňapti, in the Phug brag Kanjur. The checking of the microfiche cards
was done with the help of a simple optical means, viz. a 10 x magnifying glass.
Therefore a number of reading errors crept into the first draft; some of them
were corrected in proof-reading, but others may have survived unnoticed. The
reader is requested to communicate all mistakes he/she may detect to me and
or to the IASWR.
To several persons, acting as individuals or in the name of the institutions they
represent, I am grateful for help of various kind.
Dr. Richard A. Gard, President of the IASWR up to November 1, 1989,
acted as mediator in the first negotiations concerning the purchase of the Phug
brag Kanjur microfiche edition by the Indologisches Seminar, Bonn.
Mrs. Margaret Chen, now Vice-president and Treasurer of the IASWR,
took care of the dispatch of the microfiches and proved very efficient in pre-
paring corrected cards as substitutes for defective ones.
My sincere thanks go to Dr. Akira Yuyama, Director of the International
Institute for Buddhist Studies, Tokyo, for his interest in my plans to prepare this
"Location List" and for his willingness to get it published by his institution.
Everyone studying the Tibetan Kanjur should feel obliged to Jampa
Samten Acārya and to the persons in charge of the LTWA and the IASWR who
prepared the films, the descriptive catalogue and the microform edition of the
Phug brag Kanjur; by their efforts this important source of a collateral canonical
tradition has been made available to scholars all over the world.

Concordance
The "Concordance" adds to the concordance lines of the "Location
List" the running numbers of the texts in the Phug brag Kanjur to
which they refer
The individual entries are arranged in the order of the Phug brag
Kanjur. The "cf." used in the "Location List" for hinting at di-
vergent translations of the text concerned is not taken over into
the "Concordance".
For locating texts in the Phug brag Manuscript Kanjur with the
help of running text numbers taken from the catalogues of the
Derge (D), Tog Palace (T), Ulan Bator (U) and Peking (Q) Kanjurs
the "Keys to Concordance" are added.

Index of Tibetan Titles
Index of Tibetan Titles
The "Index of Tibetan Titles" gives the titles listed in the "Location
List" in the order of the Tibetan alphabet. Slight modifications have
been made as against the form of the titles found in the "Location
List". At the beginning of many titles the common 'Phags pa and the
classification title (viz. Dkon mchog brtsegs pa chen po' chos kyi
mam grans le'u ston phrag brgya pa las / . ) of the texts from the
Dkon brtsegs section have been omitted.

121
HELMUT EIMER (born June 14, 1936, Stettin/Pommerania)
May 31, 1967
M.A., Philosophical Faculty of Bonn University
Thesis: Der buddhistische "Weg zur Erlösung" nach indischen und tibeti-
schen Quellen,
published 1976 as: Skizzen des Erlösungsweges in buddhistischen Begriffs-
reihen.
June 19, 1974
Dr. phil., Philosophical Faculty of Bonn University
Thesis: Berichte über das Leben des Dipamkaraśrijñāna. Eine Unter-
suchung der Quellen,
published 1977 as: Berichte über das Leben des Atisa (Dipamkarasrijnana).
Eine Untersuchung der Quellen.
September 1965 to August 1968
Amanuensis at the Indologisches Seminar der Universität Bonn.
September 1968 to July 1969
Acting Research Assistant at the Indologisches Seminar der Universität
Bonn.
August 1969 to March 1986
Research scholar in the Special Research Programme on Central Asia
(Sonderforschungsbereich 12 "Zentralasien"), Bonn University.
Since April 1986
Research scholar associated with the Indologisches Seminar der
Universität Bonn.
Published books and articles (reviews not included)
Papers designated by an asterisk are reprinted in: Ein Jahrzehnt Studien zur Überlieferung
des tibetischen Kanjur, Wien 1992.
